    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6548293557152230914">Marguerite Caine's physicist parents are known for their groundbreaking achievements. Their most astonishing invention, called the Firebird, allows users to jump into multiple universes—and promises to revolutionize science forever. But then Marguerite's father is murdered, and the killer—her parent's handsome, enigmatic assistant Paul— escapes into another dimension befor</span>
  <span id="freeText6548293557152230914" style="display:none">Marguerite Caine's physicist parents are known for their groundbreaking achievements. Their most astonishing invention, called the Firebird, allows users to jump into multiple universes—and promises to revolutionize science forever. But then Marguerite's father is murdered, and the killer—her parent's handsome, enigmatic assistant Paul— escapes into another dimension before the law can touch him.<br /><br />Marguerite refuses to let the man who destroyed her family go free. So she races after Paul through different universes, always leaping into another version of herself. But she also meets alternate versions of the people she knows—including Paul, whose life entangles with hers in increasingly familiar ways. Before long she begins to question Paul's guilt—as well as her own heart. And soon she discovers the truth behind her father's death is far more sinister than she expected.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes, bloggers, librarians and other publishing professionals get early access to the book. It is a double edged in some ways because people can just p<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, bloggers, librarians and other publishing professionals get early access to the book. It is a double edged in some ways because people can just put stars without a review and that can either positively or negatively effect a book's rating. <br />I am a book blogger so am reviewing with early access. They are called advanced readers copies. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1099423362&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099423362" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16320457393061748797"><strong>Cover of my dreams, I am sorry but…DNF. At 53%.</strong><br/><br/><strong>Let me summarize you the story:</strong><br/><br/>Basically, there’s Marguerite <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415323209i/11771888._SY540_.jpg' width='500' height='550' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Paul<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415323209i/11771889._SY540_.jpg' width='500' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>And their love story.<br/><br/>Oh, and Firebirds that can transport people to alternate universes, in the background. Marguerite is searching for Paul, whom she thinks killed her father…but turns out he did not—and she believes that without any proof.<br/><br/>The romance overdrove the plot to a point that I could not take it anymore. Especially since that was not supposed to be the main element of the s</span>
  <span id="freeText16320457393061748797" style="display:none"><strong>Cover of my dreams, I am sorry but…DNF. At 53%.</strong><br><br><strong>Let me summarize you the story:</strong><br><br>Basically, there’s Marguerite <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415323209i/11771888._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Paul<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415323209i/11771889._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And their love story.<br><br>Oh, and Firebirds that can transport people to alternate universes, in the background. Marguerite is searching for Paul, whom she thinks killed her father…but turns out he did not—and she believes that without any proof.<br><br>The romance overdrove the plot to a point that I could not take it anymore. Especially since that was not supposed to be the main element of the story. And it was so predictably boring and annoying.<br><br>But, you know what? There’s actually a love-triangle. While she claims to be madly in love with Paul, there’s this Theo guy that has her attention too and with whom she flirts. <em>More than unnecessary love-triangle.</em> At least, it gets resolved…but it’s not like I’ve actually finished the book, so I might be a bad source this time.<br><br>And there’s also this weak, unnerving, difficult to like heroine called Marguerite (not fan of the name).<br><br>She’s unsupportable. Everything that comes out of her mouth is either very fake, impertinent, or totally ‘cover your eyes in shame for her’-worthy.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>It couldn’t be more obvious that my breasts are practically nonexistent, but I’m also showing off a whole lot of leg, and in the opinion of the guys in the club, that makes up for the lack of cleavage. They’re all over me, buying me drinks—more drinks I don’t need.</strong>
</blockquote><br><em>Of course, ALL OVER YOU.</em> Let’s say modesty is not her thing.<br><br>And she’s saying some stuff that perhaps are intended to make you like her more but, to me, it was only eye roll-worthy.<br><br>For instance:<br><blockquote>
  <strong>We’re pretty different, for sisters—she’s average height while I’m tall; she’s athletic while I’m anything but. She inherited our parent’s love of science and is following in Dad’s footsteps by becoming an oceanographer; I’m the odd duck in the family, the artsy one. Josie’s laid-back while I freak out about every little thing.</strong>
</blockquote><br>Ugh.Ugh.Ugh.Ugh.Ugh.<br><br>I could understand her describing the sister she loves so much – it definitely does not show in this quote – but is she obliged to compare herself?? It just makes her feel very whiny…and, if there’s something I really don’t like my heroines to be, is absolutely whiny.<br><br>Last point about the main character, she is immature and reckless! How can she expect to find and kill the man who killed her father if she doesn’t even know how?<br><br>I guess one good thing about this book is the fact that the – even though unimpressive – the world-building is well-described and we can easily understand everything about it, unlike some other books of the same genre *coughs* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17334538.Dissonance__Dissonance___1_" title="Dissonance (Dissonance, #1) by Erica O'Rourke" rel="nofollow noopener">Dissonance</a> *coughs*. But that’s definitely not a reason to actually think of upraising my rating, since I really, truly, absolutely did not enjoy it.<br><br>There’s nothing special about the writing style. It’s rather standard and similar to any random YA book you can pick up – except, of course, if the book in question you picked is Harry Potter, City of Bones, Cracked, Cruel beauty, Divergent,…which are all books I would recommend you. I will, however, not recommend you <em>this book</em>. And definitely not if you’re a fan of science fiction.<br><br><strong>This is not science fiction.</strong><br><br><strong>This is a love story.</strong><br><br><strong>To tell you the truth, I am DONE with YA romances wannabe science fiction.</strong><br><br><strong>Done.</strong><br><strong> Done.</strong><br><strong> Done.</strong><br><br><strong>No more.</strong><br><br><u>

<div id="review_998310820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/998310820" />
    <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland"><img alt="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560365354p2/21937982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/998310820?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland">Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998310820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13013643096182305863">2.5*<br/><br/>This is an interesting one to review. This is a case of this book just not being for me. It's very classic Twilight era style YA, featuring a love triangle and basically every other YA trope you can think of, including the male characters protecting the female character always *major eye roll*. That's the kind of stuff that I'm just no into anymore. Younger me would have swooned over this story, but now that I'm more of a mature reader, it doesn't appeal to me. It was too predictable, insta-</span>
  <span id="freeText13013643096182305863" style="display:none">2.5*<br /><br />This is an interesting one to review. This is a case of this book just not being for me. It's very classic Twilight era style YA, featuring a love triangle and basically every other YA trope you can think of, including the male characters protecting the female character always *major eye roll*. That's the kind of stuff that I'm just no into anymore. Younger me would have swooned over this story, but now that I'm more of a mature reader, it doesn't appeal to me. It was too predictable, insta-lovey, and just overall too haven't I read this story before?<br /><br /><b>However</b>, speaking entirely objectively, if you are into the classic style YA, which there is absolutely nothing wrong if you are you read whatever makes you happy, I think you'd really enjoy this. The whole inter dimensional time travel scifi thing was well done, and it added a cool element to the story. The love triangle wasn't the worst I've read, and the writing was solid, cliches set aside. So if you're into that, this would be a great book for you!<br /><br />I absolutely adore the covers to this trilogy, but unfortunately I just didn't enjoy it enough to want to continue. Oh well, to each their own. <br /><br />P.S. I listened to the audiobook and that made my reading experience much more enjoyable, or else this likely would have been 2/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13013643096182305863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1077758285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1077758285" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17389678-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145890p2/17389678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1077758285?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/17389678-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1077758285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11844289811376319987"><blockquote>
  <b>Technically I was the fool in this case. Here’s a tip for all you out there: read the blurb in depth because your cause of complaint may actually have no merit.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I happily allowed myself to be deceived. <b>Do you or do you not see that brilliantly crafted cover. </b>I’m going to go ahead and make a grand exclamation: <b>that may just be the most beauteous cover of 2014. </b>Watercolours, reflections and <b>Russia</b> (which I love, setting wise)—it’s everything Jess could ever ask for. And that blurb. We’re promis</span>
  <span id="freeText11844289811376319987" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>Technically I was the fool in this case. Here’s a tip for all you out there: read the blurb in depth because your cause of complaint may actually have no merit.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I happily allowed myself to be deceived. <b>Do you or do you not see that brilliantly crafted cover. </b>I’m going to go ahead and make a grand exclamation: <b>that may just be the most beauteous cover of 2014. </b>Watercolours, reflections and <b>Russia</b> (which I love, setting wise)—it’s everything Jess could ever ask for. And that blurb. We’re promised a <b>chase through alternate universes. </b>That’s it. <b>I’m salivating.</b> Hand’s up if you’ve got a soft spot for parallels because holy hell, I do. So it’s looking up. The thing is, by going into this thinking,<i> “fabulous cover, the best premise in a long while and so far, great hype”</i> (as I did) you fail to read one line. And that line is <i>everything.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Marguerite is swept into an epic love affair that feels both dangerous and inevitable…</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Sometimes I read things and they just don't register with me. If I'd read that line before hand—really thought about it—I would have known what I was getting into. <br><br>Because <b>more than anything, </b><i>A Thousand Pieces of You </i>is a<b> romance. </b>We’re skipping dimensions, running across parallel universes to avenge her father’s death, <b>sure, </b>but that’s all minuscule compared to the bigger picture: <b>love. </b><br><br>Let’s rehash, shall we? Marguerite, daughter to two brilliant scientific minds, must now utilise the prototypes of her parents' Firebird device on a speed chase across dimensions in order to chase down Paul Marakov. Paul was the shy assistant to her brilliant parents who was like an adopted family member. That is, until he betrays them all. Together with Theo—other half of the assistant duo who possesses a tad more charisma—Marguerite intends to chase Paul done and avenge her father’s death. She's adamant—concentrated—up until her adventure uncovers that the truth is just buried beneath lies. Or, <b>let’s be real here,</b> until she falls in <b>love.</b><br><br>I find it so ironic that, when I read this, I’d been having a lot of conflicting thoughts about<b> love triangles </b>and<b> transcendental love.</b> Guess what? They get a special shoutout here because <b>both these feature heavily in <i>A Thousand Pieces of You</i>.</b> Let’s be honest here, two male characters were named. What else were we expecting? <b>Of course there would be a love triangle.</b> And it’s the type where we see Marguerite oscillating like a pendulum. Back and forth, <i>I love you, </i>oh but <i>I love him more. </i>Come to think of it, <i>technically, it’s a <b>love square</b></i> but you’ll have to suffer through that one on your own. I did my share already.<br><br>Instant love, this <b>isn’t,</b> per se. All three characters grew up with one another so I suppose their relationship growth occurs naturally. But in its place we have <b>transcendental love. </b>Unaware of such a concept? Well then <b>you are not missing out. </b>The short definition is this: <b>love where both characters feel blinded by their feelings, heightened by the moment and incidentally, reality is dulled and nothing else matters. </b>When you think about chasing a <i>“murderer”</i> across dimensions on a<i> clock</i>, you’d think the situation was <b>pertinent</b>. The pace is pretty much stagnant in the first half; we don’t get anywhere. It takes a chunk of the beginning to establish the situation, location and past. And even then,<i> “love” </i>comes first. In fact, even as it picks up, love still transpires. <br><br>I was confused as to how Russia would fit into the situation. I love Russia—the atmosphere, the culture, the architecture. But honestly, world building in this case was a little underdone. <b>I didn’t get the idea that we were in Russia. </b>Sure, everyone had Russian names and Russian mannerisms but it might as well have been the kingdom of France. Their journey halts for <b>three weeks </b>in this Russian rest.<b> Three weeks.</b> What I don’t understand is why Marguerite wasn’t more of a proactive character. Despite the dire situation that they're caught in, she has no sense of immediacy. But she has time for love.<b> Love, love, love. </b><br><br>Apart from that, the pace was quite fluid. It flowed well. The jump from one dimension to another was well explained. <b>The experience is wondrously portrayed.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>My hands shake as I brace myself against the brick wall.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Let's just all take a moment to appreciate that alluring first sentence. <br><br>There was however an <b>overuse of parenthesis'. </b>If you’ve read my other reviews, you’d know that I’m impartial to a good parenthesis. Oh heck, you might even say that I have quite the love affair with those brackets. But even I must say that the parenthesis was used way beyond its need. The good old bracket is used primarily for flashbacks and info dumping. With a sci-fi, the hardest bit to integrate is the science. Now, I’m no expert on science and I <b>never, ever will intend to be</b> so I can’t say to much about that. Sure, it was all very interesting but it could have been woven through in a smother manner. But I won't deny it—<b>the scientific explanations were phenomenally researched. </b>The flashbacks were also quite jarring, interrupting the fluidity of the tale; we could've used without the parenthesis'. I’ve read many a book where there was a need for asides, but never have they been put in a parenthesis before (or at least not in great chunks. Hey, the irony of the bracket is before me.) It was an odd element and could make or break it for many. <br><br>While the world building was fantastic, I felt a complete disconnection to the characters. What made them different from everyone else? There weren't any <i>unique </i>characteristics and I just couldn't find Marguerite’s <i>distinctive</i> voice. The love triangle is also composed up of two generic love interests. It's been done before. Granted, it is a foolproof method, but that's just it; it's conventional and if you're seeking something more <i>profound </i>then perhaps this isn't for you. <br><br>There’s also an abundance of pop culture references. For those who yearn a lifeline to reality then this is for you—we’ve got Brad Pitt and Jennifer Anniston, Siri herself, Dicaprio gets a shoutout. However, I can also see this aspect being a cause of confusion for many. Pop culture is a hard element to judge. There will always be those who love it and those who detest it. Personally, it didn’t bother me. In fact, I love a good pop culture reference, but <b>only when done satirically. </b>In this case, pop culture is utilised in order to establish a link with the reader's present; to forge a connection between the audience and the book. We even got a Beyonce reference. Marguerite fancies herself to be quite the spirit animal of Queen B. And I’m not talking in terms of girl power (that would be admirable). <br><br>So I’m caught, you see. <b>It was a solid start to the beginning of a new series. </b>But if you want prose, that ease that often comes with relationship dynamics, and a handful of good metaphors then you will be sorely disappointed. <b>A <i>Thousand Pieces of You </i>is a brilliant read for all those who love their sci-fi with a less sci and a little more <u>fire.</u></b> It’s a<b>
  <u> romance </u>
</b>lover’s <i>
  <u>dream,</u>
</i> this, and an interesting take on dimension travelling. <br><br>Ultimately I fell into the first category. While Marguerite’s overarching aim was justice for her father, often he got left behind in her journey to love. It’s a shame that I cared not for the romance. It was sweet but they were <b>characters that we’ve seen time and time again;</b> the brooding, shy and quiet boy versus the wild, loud and charismatic bad boy vying for one girl’s heart. The concept was brilliant and the setting was an interesting choice, so here’s to a series that will hopefully <b>dial down on the proclamations of love </b>and get into the nitty gritty. We’ve got <b>great potential for a story concerning mixed morals and grey areas</b> but unfortunately A <i>Thousand Pieces of You</i> just does not deliver. <br><br><i>Many thanks to publisher for providing a review copy in exchange for an honest review. </i><br><br><blockquote>_________________________________</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>Sometimes I think: <i>Perhaps you're being too hard on these books. Why are you a picky reader? Maybe you should stop overthinking things?</i> </blockquote><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413339531ra/11498818.gif" width="459" height="352" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Who do I kid? <b>This had problems.</b> And I shall pull it apart to show you. So you know the drill. <b>Review to come.</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11844289811376319987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_939243187" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939243187" />
    <a title="Tess Burton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4098917-tess-burton"><img alt="Tess Burton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593448934p2/4098917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939243187?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tess Burton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tess Burton" href="/user/show/4098917-tess-burton">Tess Burton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=romantic-subplot">romantic-subplot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=sci-fi-or-futuristic">sci-fi-or-futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939243187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer760565646683338991"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398549i/770407._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='30' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>**Minor Spoilers**<br/><br/>I've pulled up my ranty-pants, I'm fuelled by rage and coffee, let's kick this review off with a summary of my reading experience, shall we?<br/><br/>To my great displeasure, <strong>reading this book was like chewing on a lump of black mould just to check it ain't caviar</strong>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415293931ra/11766390.gif' alt='' width='250' height='231' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><strong>I mean</strong>, <em>what the ever-loving bejesus <strong>was that</strong></em>?<br/><br/>It was <strong>not </strong>supposed to be like this. You don't understand; <strong>I was excited</strong>. I've had my eye on this for <strong>months</strong>. This was supposed to be epic, I honestly had no doubts. With the premis</span>
  <span id="freeText760565646683338991" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398549i/770407._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="30" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>**Minor Spoilers**<br><br>I've pulled up my ranty-pants, I'm fuelled by rage and coffee, let's kick this review off with a summary of my reading experience, shall we?<br><br>To my great displeasure, <strong>reading this book was like chewing on a lump of black mould just to check it ain't caviar</strong>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415293931ra/11766390.gif" alt="" width="250" height="231" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>I mean</strong>, <em>what the ever-loving bejesus <strong>was that</strong></em>?<br><br>It was <strong>not </strong>supposed to be like this. You don't understand; <strong>I was excited</strong>. I've had my eye on this for <strong>months</strong>. This was supposed to be epic, I honestly had no doubts. With the premise being a daughter of two scientists chasing her father's killer through <em>alternate dimensions</em> in order to exact her revenge, <strong>
  <em>how can you fuck up</em>
</strong>?<br><br>There is <strong>nothing</strong> redeemable about this book. I could scrape the bottom of the barrel if I really tried, but what would be the point? I would be saying things like <em>at least it didn't condone rape!</em> or <em>hey, spelling errors were not abundant in this novel, thumbs up! </em>And anyway, I don't want to deny myself the pleasure of rage-reviewing this hunk o' crap into next Tuesday.<br><br>We begin with Marguerite (solid name), the daughter of two genius scientists who have invented the Firebird, a device that allows the user to jump into the body of their alternate self in an alternate universe. Marguerite wants to murder the man who killed her father and stole one of the Firebird prototypes to escape to another dimension, so she intends to follow him and<strong> totally kill him</strong>. Unfortunately, the girl is not exactly filled with blood-lust, so it's pretty obvious from the start that she's not going to kill him<br><br>Now, when dealing with sci-fi alternate reality whatsits and a plot that could potentially create some pretty intricate plot holes, it's a good idea to properly explain <strong>how yo shit works</strong>. The best explanation in the book is literally where the author explains what an alternate dimension is.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"These dimensions aren't off in faraway outer space. They're literally all around us, even within us, but because they exist in another reality, we can't perceive them."</em>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415293931ra/11766391.gif" alt="" width="500" height="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's a bad copy-paste from a child's guide to quantum physics. <em>We all know what an alternate universe is, you plum</em>. What we would like, Claudia Gray, is a decent explanation of how you've made dimension leaping possible, how it all works, what happens when you get there. But what do we get? <strong>A series of cop-outs</strong>.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"When people travel through dimensions." he said, staring down at the prototypes, "they leave traces. Subatomic - okay, I'm gonna cut to the chase. The point is, I can go after Paul."</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>"The devices have to be made out of specific materials that move much more easily than other forms of matter; they have to anchor the consciousness of the traveler, which is apparently very difficult; and about a million other technical considerations I'd have to get umpteen physics degrees to even understand. Long story short: the devices are really hard to make."</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>"So does destiny create the math, or does math create our destiny?"</em>
  <br>
  <em> "Insufficient data," Paul said.</em>
</blockquote><br>This <em>screams</em> laziness. It's the type of world-building that I hate: <em>this device does this because I say so</em>, <em>I need my plot to work so just go with it</em>. <strong>HELL NO</strong>. How can I get into a story when you're making it so difficult?!<br><br>Nevertheless, I carried on reading. I hadn't seen any dimension leaps yet, and I was sure they were going to be good. Remember <em>Family Guy</em>'s dimension leaping episode? Remember <em>Red Dwarf</em>'s? They were <strong>brilliant</strong>, and that's what I thought<em> A Thousand Pieces of You</em> was going to be like. The creative possibilities are truly endless.<br><br>In total, Marguerite jumps to four different dimensions.<br><br>1. A world where she lives in London because her family all died. This London is exactly the same as our London, only we all have holographic smartphone wristwatches with tracking technology and you can electrify an attacker with a ring. <strong>That's it</strong>.<br><br>2. A world where technology didn't advance so quick and her mother's ancestors never immigrated from Russia so for some reason now she's a Russian princess for no other reason than it would be cool to be a princess. <strong>That's it</strong>.<br><br>3. A world where<strong> literally everything is the same</strong> but her dad is alive.<br><br>4. A world where the sea levels rose faster than our world so she lives underwater &amp; her family are oceanologists and still alive.<br><br><strong>There is literally nothing else</strong>.<br><br>Where's the imagination?! Where did the potential go?! What happened to my perfect expectation of dazzling, intricate and clever dimensions?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415293931ra/11766393.gif" alt="" width="500" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These new worlds really just focused on how Marguerite's life was different, and didn't give a crap about the rest of the world. And that wouldn't be so bad if they were <strong>remotely interesting</strong>. I'm reminded of the film <em>Bedazzled</em>, wherein Brendan Fraser continues to make deals with the devil to change his life, and he goes through some <em>brilliant</em> changes in identity that lead to hilarity as the devil keeps screwing him over.<br><br><a href="https://tessburton.files.wordpress.com/2014/11/309823146d9e082334f1494036599be6-0.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415293931i/11766394.jpg" alt="309823146d9e082334f1494036599be6-0" width="500" height="212" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>That is how you do it, but do we get that? <strong>Fuck no</strong>. The only new life which was even <em>slightly</em> interesting was when Marguerite ended up a Russian princess. And even that was crossing a line. A princess? <em>Really</em>? Why is that grandeur necessary? Plus, why on earth isn't she obsessed with finding out <em>how</em>, in this reality, she's fucking royalty? The only "explanation" we get is that her mum's ancestors were Russian. <strong>THAT IS IT</strong>. I swear, the only reason she added the princess element was for the romantic subplot involving a royal guard, who just so happens to be the alternate version of the guy who she believes killed her dad. Who she's also in love with. Because why not add a <em>forbidden love</em> element to the already <em>transcendental love</em> element you've already got going on? <em>Awww they keep finding each other in alternate universes</em>. How fucking poetic and not at all a rip-off of <em>Cloud Atlas</em>. Oh and there's a love triangle, because the forbidden transcendental love story wasn't epic enough. No, these two have to put all other couples to shame.<br><br>I just <em>
  <strong>can't</strong>
</em> with this novel. I can't. I'm so disappointed. I'm so sad about it all. No glorious alternate universes, no clever changes of identity, just a romp through reality having to endure naive little Marguerite not giving a shit about stuff that should be important and awkwardly flirting with two men. The plot would have been <strong>fine</strong> (aside from the plothole-ish ending) if it wasn't completely overshadowed with unfulfilled potential and an unnecessary obsession with the love story. It's a miracle I didn't mind the characters, otherwise you'd be in for another paragraph ranting about how shit they were. They were developed enough for me not to have a problem with them, I'll say that. Though Marguerite's incessant pop culture references really grated my cheese.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"Conley gets this look on his face, like I'm so cute, like a GIF of baby puppies or something."</em>
</blockquote><br>This book failed on every level for me. It was a book I had such high hopes for and it pissed in the face of every last one, leaving me wishing I had been born in a dimension where this piece of shit had never been written.</span>
  <a data-text-id="760565646683338991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1503978106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1503978106" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1503978106?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1503978106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5398601057758407640">me: i have sooo many series that i have started and really need to finish.<br/>also me: i should start a new series.<br/><br/>i have had this book sitting on my bookshelf for ages now, so i suppose it was finally time to pick it up (sorry to the other series that need to be completed). and im so happy i did because i really enjoyed this!!<br/><br/>im pretty sure ive never read anything quite like this storyline before, so i was very eager to dive right into something so fresh and unique. and it really delivered. i thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText5398601057758407640" style="display:none">me: i have sooo many series that i have started and really need to finish.<br />also me: i should start a new series.<br /><br />i have had this book sitting on my bookshelf for ages now, so i suppose it was finally time to pick it up (sorry to the other series that need to be completed). and im so happy i did because i really enjoyed this!!<br /><br />im pretty sure ive never read anything quite like this storyline before, so i was very eager to dive right into something so fresh and unique. and it really delivered. i thought the whole concept of multiple universes was effectively explained. it was introduced in a really easy way to where i didnt feel like i had to think through all the science, which i appreciated. and the world building in each of the different universes was also really well done. i honestly didnt like marguerite and the love triangle didnt really do anything for me, but i thought the plot was just so interesting that i had to keep reading. some parts were a bit predictable, but it didnt detract from my overall enjoyment of the story. <br /><br />i also thought this book was paced really well and set up for the sequel quite nicely. everything was wrapped up, but still open-ended enough to make me want to pick up the second book. no cliffhanger in sight, thank goodness. so i would say this was a really strong start to what i hope will be an amazing series!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18233477037354521934"><u> <i> Alternative titles for this masterpiece: </i> </u><br/><br/>-	<i> A Thousand Pieces of My Shattered Heart </i><br/>-	<i> A Thousand Reasons to Love Paul Markov </i><br/>-	<i> A Thousand Moments of Pain and Happiness </i><br/><br/>This book was bloody brilliant!! Claudia Gray has spun a gorgeous tale that is dazzling, intense, and so fricken enjoyable to read! <br/><br/>This book has it all; dimension travel, a lesson in physics, heart-stalling plot twists, family values, and a precious love interest that has stolen my heart. And I mean look at that cover, it’s </span>
  <span id="freeText18233477037354521934" style="display:none"><u> <i> Alternative titles for this masterpiece: </i> </u><br><br>-	<i> A Thousand Pieces of My Shattered Heart </i><br>-	<i> A Thousand Reasons to Love Paul Markov </i><br>-	<i> A Thousand Moments of Pain and Happiness </i><br><br>This book was bloody brilliant!! Claudia Gray has spun a gorgeous tale that is dazzling, intense, and so fricken enjoyable to read! <br><br>This book has it all; dimension travel, a lesson in physics, heart-stalling plot twists, family values, and a precious love interest that has stolen my heart. And I mean look at that cover, it’s bloody gorgeous!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471608224ra/20079065.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So the whole physics behind the dimension travel had my head spinning (I’m not planning on majoring in science, can you tell?) but the author broke it down quite nicely that even <i> I </i> could understand. <br><br>And the Russiaverse, can we just talk about how perfect it is?? <br><br>Damn, the characters travel through dimensions often enough but the world building was create so seamless; is this woman even real???<br><br><i> “Every form of art is another way of seeing the world. Another perspective, another window. And science –that’s the most spectacular window of all. You can see the entire universe from there.” </i> <br><br>Now as cute as I <i> thought </i> this book was, there’s some killer heartbreaking moment, so prepare yourself, kids. <br><br>And I know, I know, the whole <b> <i> love triangle </i> </b> trope sets alarm bells off for everyone, but AS MUCH AS I <b> DETES </b> love triangles, I didn’t find this one, <b> terrible. </b> Actually, I feel like it was done well in comparison to the other love triangles I’ve had to trudge through in my many years. <br><br>Anyways, read this, it’s great, it’s awesome, it’s fantastic, it’s beautiful.<br><br>And if that didn’t convince you. . .<br>. . . do if for my child, Paul Markov.<br><br><br><i> “I have no need for a world without you in it.” </i> <br><br>*screams for ten decades* <br><br><br>4.5 stars!!!<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br><i> <b> Buddy read </b> with the lovely, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/56485897-alyssa" rel="nofollow noopener">Alyssa</a> </i></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1842297043?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1842297043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer869864693587053682">This book is one of the fastest paced books I have ever read. Usually, an author will take chapter or 2 to introduce the background of the story but this book just immediately starts off at the plot, but it also doesn't confuse you. I really liked the world Claudia Gray built and the 'Firebird' concept was very well written. The inter-dimensional travel is a very crucial element of the plot and is focused on heavily, which is fascinating. <br/><br/>Marguerite's parents are physicists who have successfully</span>
  <span id="freeText869864693587053682" style="display:none">This book is one of the fastest paced books I have ever read. Usually, an author will take chapter or 2 to introduce the background of the story but this book just immediately starts off at the plot, but it also doesn't confuse you. I really liked the world Claudia Gray built and the 'Firebird' concept was very well written. The inter-dimensional travel is a very crucial element of the plot and is focused on heavily, which is fascinating. <br /><br />Marguerite's parents are physicists who have successfully created a machine (Firebird) that allows people to jump into another dimension. Each dimension is a reflection of possibilities that could have taken place in our world. Some dimensions are very similar to ours, while some are completely exotic. Our protagonist sets out on a mission to find the person who murdered her father and is planning her parent's downfall. <br />As I mentioned the inter-dimensional travel is very openly exhibited aspect and protagonist jumps into not just one but many dimensions, in which she discover the many paths her world could have taken.<br />I really enjoyed this book and finished it in one sitting. The plot grows thicker as we delve deeper into the book and Claudia Gray does a great job in creating the Firebird element of the story. I love the plot and I rate this book 4.5 stars.<br />The cover of this book is <b>BEAUTIFUL</b> and represents not only 2 different dimensions but also our protagonists love for art, so great job on that front.</span>
  <a data-text-id="869864693587053682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_771271718" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/771271718" />
    <a title="Taschima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima"><img alt="Taschima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574541558p2/2435020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/771271718?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taschima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taschima" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima">Taschima</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435020-taschima?shelf=e-arc-titles-to-review">e-arc-titles-to-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer771271718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1575471708883955415">Sometimes, all you can do is cry happy tears. I mean, look at that cover, it is incredible. All I wanted was for the story between the pages to be just as good, to live up not only to the awesome cover design but to the hype. And man, did it deliver.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408510821ra/10858134.gif' width='350' height='175' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I think A Thousand Pieces of You is definitely my favorite Claudia Gray book. It kind of reminds me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays' title='All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill' rel='nofollow noopener'>All Our Yesterdays</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17334538.Dissonance__Dissonance___1_' title='Dissonance (Dissonance, #1) by Erica O'Rourke' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dissonance</a>. It is an intricate story that keeps you on your toes. Since the beginning of the story me and my friend Lexie we</span>
  <span id="freeText1575471708883955415" style="display:none">Sometimes, all you can do is cry happy tears. I mean, look at that cover, it is incredible. All I wanted was for the story between the pages to be just as good, to live up not only to the awesome cover design but to the hype. And man, did it deliver.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408510821ra/10858134.gif" width="350" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think A Thousand Pieces of You is definitely my favorite Claudia Gray book. It kind of reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill" rel="nofollow noopener">All Our Yesterdays</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17334538.Dissonance__Dissonance___1_" title="Dissonance (Dissonance, #1) by Erica O'Rourke" rel="nofollow noopener">Dissonance</a>. It is an intricate story that keeps you on your toes. Since the beginning of the story me and my friend Lexie were trying to guess the ending, the bad guy, and the romantic interest (I know, we are bad). While some things we got figured out pretty quickly others came as a surprise. Good Claudia Gray, you kept me guessing!<br><br><b>
  <i>"I don't know if I'm the kind of person who can kill a man in cold blood. But I'm going to find out."</i>
</b><br><br>The beginning of the novel is fast, interesting, and it gets your blood pumping. First thing to come up: Murder. Revenge. Meg is out for blood. Paul's blood to be exact. She believes he killed her father and then ran off with her parent's prized experiment; a machine that can travel through dimensions. So Meg, with a little help from her friend Theo, is out to get Paul and make him pay.<br><br><b>
  <i>"The universe is in fact a multiverse. Countless dimensions exist, all layered within one another.<br>Each dimension represents one set of possibilities. Essentially, everything that can happen does happen... Every possibility, every time fate flips a coin, splits the dimensions yet again, creating yet more layer of reality. It goes on and on forever, to infinity."</i>
</b><br><br>Meg is the odd one out in her family, but that doesn't mean she is alone. Her entire family is creative of a sort, they just use different hemispheres of their brains to get the job done. Her parents and big sister are into science while Meg is into art. This makes her likable, being the odd man out. She is also ballsy. From pretty early on you get the picture she knows next about nothing regarding what exactly the device her parent's made to cross dimensions does but she still risks it in order to find her father's supposed murderer. All in all I really liked her. She is shown to be conflicted throughout the read and to really take to heart every single version of herself she falls into. <br><br>I can't talk much about specific things like the romance because it would just give too much away. All I can really say is that the romance aspect is a BIG part of A Thousand Pieces of You, and that is just dandy. It is a really juicy, edge of your seat kind of romance. There is one dimension that is set in Russia that is BOUND to hook readers. If you were a little "eh" when starting the read when you get to the Russian side of the story you will be hooked forevermore. It was my favorite part and completely brought the book to a whole new level.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["I fell in love with one Paul. I fell in love with his unchanging soul. Does that mean I fell in love with every Paul, everywhere?" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>A Thousand Pieces of You is a must read this year. The pretty cover does meet the expectations. If you liked the Evernight series by Claudia, then you will love this one. I liked Evernight, but I LOVED A Thousand Pieces of You and I can't wait for the sequel!<br><br>Old Update:<br><br><b>THAT COVER </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400190224ra/9646545.gif" width="200" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1575471708883955415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1672661692" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1672661692" />
    <a title="Helen 2.0" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0"><img alt="Helen 2.0" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553725p2/39575951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672661692?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=read-16">read-16</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=cover-candy">cover-candy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672661692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9260574928980944781">3.5 <blockquote>
<i>"You are not my Marguerite. And yet, you are. This essential thing you share - your soul - </i>that<i> is what I love. <br/>I would love you in any shape, in any world, with any past. Never doubt that."</i>
</blockquote><br/>A Thousand Pieces of You is a book with a 5-star premise, unfortunately laden with a few core issues that drag down my rating. Marguerite is the daughter of two genius physicists inventing a machine that allows consciousness to jump through parallel universes. Meg's father is killed for his research, so</span>
  <span id="freeText9260574928980944781" style="display:none">3.5 <blockquote>
<i>"You are not my Marguerite. And yet, you are. This essential thing you share - your soul - </i>that<i> is what I love. <br>I would love you in any shape, in any world, with any past. Never doubt that."</i>
</blockquote><br>A Thousand Pieces of You is a book with a 5-star premise, unfortunately laden with a few core issues that drag down my rating. Marguerite is the daughter of two genius physicists inventing a machine that allows consciousness to jump through parallel universes. Meg's father is killed for his research, so she and her <s>boytoy</s> friend Theo track the killer across dimensions. Things escalate romantically; action-wise, not so much.<br><br>The fun part of this book is the soap opera shitstorm that results from interdimensional love triangles. Imagine falling for a person in one dimension, then meeting a different version of him/her in another dimension. So, who are you in love with now? One? Both? Neither? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Exhibit A: <i>Paul rubs my back, slow and gentle, comforting me as I struggle against tears and think of the Paul I lost. Am I betraying him now? Or am I being a fool, because the man I loved has basically come back to life and I can't love him again?</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is superfood for drama, and double it because there are two love interests. Basically, I came for the premise but stuck around for the relationships.<br><br>The plot structure needed some work. In a book that takes place not only in several different settings, but several different <i>universes</i>, the plot is bound to be put on hold for explanations every now and then. But Gray attempted to force so many infodumps and lapses between the action (especially in earlier chapters) that the book really dragged sometimes. Perhaps the story would have benefited from hints of info dropped along the adventure, rather than pages and pages of flashbacks/boring text.<br><br>Plot content was also lacking - mostly because some major points <b>didn't make any damn sense.</b> Take the villain, for example: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Wyatt Conley tries to blackmail Meg's family so that he can send spies and start wars in other dimensions. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480114736ra/21275623.gif" height="250" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Where's the motive? What is there to gain from a venture like that? If this was explained in A Thousand Pieces of You at all, then not well enough.<br>Also, Meg's extraordinary abilities when it comes to interdimensional travel - the way these are explained away is really lazy and questionable. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Conley manages to stash a device that can superify people (which he obtained from God knows where) in Meg's living room. The four most knowledgeable people on devices like that FAIL to notice it's dangerous and it goes off right when Meg and only Meg is in the room. Oh, and it can never be used again, because, like, reasons. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482077721i/21482181._SY540_.jpg" height="300" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I call bullshit.<br><br><b>Is the series worth continuing? I'm in need of some advice here.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9260574928980944781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1435156385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1435156385" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1435156385?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062278975" href="/book/show/25816876-a-thousand-pieces-of-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435156385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13470580368588155653">BECAUSE THIS COVER *drops dead*<br/><br/><b>"Eventually you'll get used to the pain. You'll forget who you were without it; you'll forget what you looked like without your scars.”</b><br/><br/>I premit that I am <u>perfectly aware of the scientific and logical nonsense present in this book, some of which I consider unforgivable</u>. But this story had me hooked, it thrilled and excited me, it's <b>well-written</b>, <b>compelling</b>, <b>wonderfully crafted</b>, and I enjoyed it more than not. And, ultimately, that's always what matters the most. To </span>
  <span id="freeText13470580368588155653" style="display:none">BECAUSE THIS COVER *drops dead*<br /><br /><b>"Eventually you'll get used to the pain. You'll forget who you were without it; you'll forget what you looked like without your scars.”</b><br /><br />I premit that I am <u>perfectly aware of the scientific and logical nonsense present in this book, some of which I consider unforgivable</u>. But this story had me hooked, it thrilled and excited me, it's <b>well-written</b>, <b>compelling</b>, <b>wonderfully crafted</b>, and I enjoyed it more than not. And, ultimately, that's always what matters the most. To me, at least.<br /><br />To begin with, I love science-fiction. I love, like, <i>totally crazy for it</i>. And I'm not talking exactly about spaceships and green aliens; I am talking about the kind of things that <i>A Thousand Pieces of You</i> offers. <b>New technologies</b>. <b>Made-up explanations for the said devices/discoveries built upon incontrovertible scientific truths</b>, and<b>complex plots</b> that put into play their practical implementations. If it comes with all the related<b> set of thorny ethical issues</b>, then, all the better.<br /><br />•The thing is, the more complex the <b>science </b>you put into play, the harder it is to be coherent and aware of all of the consequences that the strict applications of that concept may and must have. If you tell a story about a world in which gravity works the other way around, you cannot assume that Newton discovered it thanks to an apple fallen from a tree. If in the world you're building <b>objects, namely, everything having mass</b>, cannot be moved from a dimension to the other, you cannot in any way assume that the object used to move a coscience from a dimension to the other -the <b>Firebird</b>- can move along with it.<br />Is this that hard to grasp?<br />But I get that this whole book wouldn't have been written without this "oversight", so let's bend the rules of physics to make the story work. Why bother to come up with a rational explanation for it when no one will notice?<br /><b>I noticed</b>. Sorry.<br /><br />And speaking about matter, <b>let's talk about the bodies</b> (I'm not doing any spoiler, since we know since the very first page and before that this book wheels around interdimensional journeys). <br />When a person uses the Firebird to jump into another dimension, it's only their coscience, a form of energy, according to Gray's point of view, that travels, not the body, which, as I said, can't be moved through different dimensions being made of matter. But then, what happens to it when the coscience is gone? Gray says it becomes <b>'no longer observable'</b>, calling upon the <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IOYyCHGWJq4" rel="nofollow noopener">Schrödinger's cat</a>, choice that I find a leeettle bit gratuitous, but yes, okay, let's go with it. In practice, a no longer observable object is there, but you don't see it unless someone else who can draws your attention to it. Now, my point is, even if you can't see it, the body is still there, and when Marguerite leaves for the first time she's sitting on the steps of her home's deck. Honestly, how many chances are there that nobody stumbled on her in almost a month she was gone? And moreover: while the coscience is away, its body's heart is pumping? Its lungs are working? If it is so, what about food? How can an empty body survive that long without nourishment?<br />I'm sorry, I really enjoyed this story, truly, but I can't honestly get past holes like this. If a scientific background has to be created,<b> it must be done properly</b>.<br /><br />I'm done with the technobabble, I promise. It's just that <b>I expected much, much more from this point of view</b>.<br /><br />•The <b>plot</b> on the contrary, was an utterly <b>delightful surprise</b>. Fast-paced and far, far more <b>entagled</b> than I had guessed at first glance. I truly appreciated the various twists, although I had predicted some of them. The <b> writing</b> is also another strong point, undoubtely: magnetic and delicate, sensitive and deep. Sometimes it was as soft as a melody, and I lost myself in it. It's not always at its best, but its quality is always good.<br /><br />•The <b>main character</b>, Marguerite, is not irritiating nor totally idiotic, but questionable indeed she is. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I can't wrap my mind about how could she spend the night with a man while in the body of another of her selves. It's not said out of prudishness or what you want to call it, it's just that, hello, that's not your body. It's not yours to use that way. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, I found her to be a little slow in some moments and a little silly in others, but nothing over which I can't get. <br /><br />•And, yes, I regret to have to tell you so, but there is a <b>love triangle</b>. It's not as overwhelming as you may think, though -even because it's pretty clear from the beginning who she'll end up with- and towards the end the author manages it in a way I definitely appreciated. It ruined my enjoyment only a little; I've seen far worse. Besides, I liked (and swooned over) Paul, so, yup, for the love story it's a yes.<br /><br />In a nutshell, this book is <b>far from perfect</b>, and these three words are the ones I would probably choose to describe it as briefly as I could. <b>But there is a thread of poetry interwoven in this story's weave, and I can't ignore it, not even in the face of all its flaws</b>. What I loved about it is that it is a book about <b>love</b>: and not merely the love we harbor for our dear ones, but the one some people harbor towards science, and the one others harbor towards arts too. And speaking about the latter two, you know... I've never been so sure they are totally different one from the other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13470580368588155653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1899823601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1899823601" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1899823601?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1899823601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15285692419836984865"><i>That's it. I'm starting a campaign to end love triangles as a staple of the Young Adult genre.</i> Or I'd like to anyway, but you know, I've got a lot of books to read. <br/><br/>I'll admit it, I'm kind of scared to review this one because so many of my friends LOVED this, but I was let down...<br/><br/>Those of you who have followed me for any length of time know that one of my biggest pet peeves are love triangles. I get why authors feel the need to include them. Romance adds a bit of sizzle to the middle of a book w</span>
  <span id="freeText15285692419836984865" style="display:none"><i>That's it. I'm starting a campaign to end love triangles as a staple of the Young Adult genre.</i> Or I'd like to anyway, but you know, I've got a lot of books to read. <br><br>I'll admit it, I'm kind of scared to review this one because so many of my friends LOVED this, but I was let down...<br><br>Those of you who have followed me for any length of time know that one of my biggest pet peeves are love triangles. I get why authors feel the need to include them. Romance adds a bit of sizzle to the middle of a book where the plot feels a bit slow. However, it's when the main plot starts getting overtaken by the relationship dynamics between the characters that I start getting frustrated<b> because that's when the action also starts suffering.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489259775ra/22200415.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's especially frustrating considering that this book has such a strong opening and close. You hit the ground running with the characters from page one, setting the expectation that this was going to be fast paced universe jumping - which I was <u>totally</u> down for! What I got instead was a slow burn love triangle as Marguerite decides which boy she likes the most and can trust the most, which was repeated in each universe and in my opinion killed the pacing. <br><br>I think it's important to consider plot as context for relationships in the first place, because <i>there is a time and place for romance.</i><br><br><b>I don't know about you, but if my father had just been MURDERED and I wasn't sure which of my friends did it, romancing either of them would be the last thing on my mind.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412071927ra/11319711.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Of course, we can't talk about love triangles without talking about the motivations of female characters. I love kickass female heroines in novels, television shows and movies. My favorite characters are the women with agency, who effect the plot and don't let external plot devices (such as men) affect them. <b>Unfortunately, Marguerite just isn't one of those characters.</b><br><br>Her narrative point of view centers almost totally around men! Each time she jumps into another universe, instead of learning about the new world she's in, Marguerite immediately starts thinking about boys. And lets face it: <b>her reasons for trusting both Theo and Paul in the first place are flimsy at best and ludicrous at worst.</b><br><br>For example, she immediately trusts one of the two because <i>his eyes look sad when she sees him.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489263673ra/22200783.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>In my opinion, this novel would have benefited in a big way from shelving the romantic love triangle entirely, in favor of fleshing out the different universes and the larger mystery around Marguerite's father. <br><br>It was still a fun and quick read, and I commend Claudia Gray for creating different worlds that I would have loved to have seen more of. <b>The ending gave me hope that the next book will improve on the areas I took issue with here, so I'll be continuing with the next book soon</b> while maintaining my zeal for stronger focuses on plot in YA and less on forced romantic triangles. <br><br>#Downwithlovetrianges<br>#morestrongfemaleMCsplease<br><br>★★★✩✩ = 3 average, hoping-for-better-in-the-sequel, stars<br><br>This review and more can be found on my blog: <a href="https://bookbastion.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Bastion</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15285692419836984865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
