  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1734723687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1734723687" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1734723687?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1734723687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11739042029479882303"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Every form of art is another way of seeing the world. Another perspective, another window. And science –that’s the most spectacular window of all. You can see the entire universe from there.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Marguerite Caine is known to be the daughter of the famous achievers who built a invention together called the Firebird, a creation that allows one to jump into different dimensions, different universes, different worlds. Her father, Henry Caine, was an English man who was the only one to believe </span>
  <span id="freeText11739042029479882303" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Every form of art is another way of seeing the world. Another perspective, another window. And science –that’s the most spectacular window of all. You can see the entire universe from there.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Marguerite Caine is known to be the daughter of the famous achievers who built a invention together called the Firebird, a creation that allows one to jump into different dimensions, different universes, different worlds. Her father, Henry Caine, was an English man who was the only one to believe Sophia, his wife and Marguerite's mother, which is part of the reason they met and fell in love. But out of nowhere, one day, Henry is murdered and the believed suspect is Paul, Sophia and Henry's trusted assistant who graduated high school at the age of 13 and is known to be one of the only ones to know about this invention called the Firebird. Paul, who is the one Marguerite suspects as the killer, escapes into another dimension like he learned to do so before anyone can touch him, including Marguerite, Theo, one of her best and most trusted friends, and the law. Knowing Marguerite wants vengeance for what happened to her father, she does not give up and decides to go with Theo by jumping into these different worlds to find Paul and make him pay for what he did. As Marguerite meets different versions of herself and goes along the lines, she also meets different versions of people she knows including Paul, Theo, her mother, and even her father. But sometimes, things aren't always as one believes it to be, and Marguerite begins to doubt her suspicion and finds out the truth about her father's murder.<br /><br />I was told by a friend of mine that Spain changed me since I was over there for a month and did not read at all, so maybe that has to do with it? But at the same time, I don't believe that. Spain really has nothing to do with this. I was excited to be back home because I was finally able to read, but then I come back to read books and check out books from the library only to not enjoy one. <i>A Thousand Pieces of You</i> has been on my TBR for quite some time. I tried reading it last year but never finished it because I was bored on the very first pages. This time, I forced myself to continue, and I kind of regret it.<br /><br />The premise of this books sounded so interesting to me. I knew about the love triangle that goes on in the whole series, or just the 2 books, but I completely ignored that, even though it's one of my biggest book pet peeves. I mean, a girl who wants to take revenge on someone she thought she loved because she thinks he killed her father? I was so drawn into the whole thing, but I guess, <b>some things are never what one thinks they are.</b> Again, I was bored the whole time reading this. I was even gonna get book 2 of this but I decided not to since I wasn't sure if I was gonna enjoy this or not. I guess I didn't enjoy the characters, but I also didn't enjoy the plot. While the plot is what the synopsis offers, at the same time, it isn't. Claudia Gray isn't an author for me. I ended up marking her recent book, <i>Defy the Stars</i>, as a DNF and failed BR because I was so bored the whole time that I totally forgot I owned the book and was reading it with 4 other friends. A Thousand Pieces of You was no different to me. I was bored the whole time and even on around page 330, as things were making sense and as I predicted, I was bored and upset with everything. I should've just left the book as a DNF, but I guess her writing was addicting since it was easy to follow the story and the writing.<br /><br />The characters were something else I didn't enjoy reading about. I didn't trust either guy in the beginning, not Paul nor Theo, but then I began trusting one of them and not the other, and even though I hate predicting, I predicted the guy I couldn't trust was really <b>someone I couldn't trust,</b> and I didn't like that. The romance in this was something I didn't like either, ignoring the love triangle, because the whole dimensions thing was honeslty messing with my head and fucking me up. Marguerite loved a guy in one dimension but wasn't sure of <i>her guy</i> in <i>her world</i> and I was so confused because even though it wasn't the same person, <b>it was still the same person at the same time.</b> Her whole love-interest was just messing with my head. I won't say she time traveled, but she went to a different dimension to Russia and it was different than the dimension she went to in London. I know it's Russia in London, but one was present year and the other was like, the 1900's or something. It was most likely that, or maybe this just didn't make sense to me. Talking about London and Russia, <b>there was no world building.</b> Again, another world building fail, or was it just me that didn't see it? We got information on technology and why London has this and that and Russia doesn't because this and that, but why exactly did <b>London have something that Russia didn't and Russia didn't have something while London did?</b> There was no world building and explanations on the different worlds, on the present and past worlds. First, Marguerite goes to London to find Paul but London is so advanced in technology while her "real" world isn't, then she's suddenly a princess in Russia and the tsar is her father and she's called <i>Imperial Highness,</i> then she's in her own world but her dad is alive and she's got a little differences in her room and house here and there, and she's able to live underwater and be in a submarine because her parents are studying Oceanology as well so she knows about the ocean and sea and all that.<br /><br />Every dimension felt the same to me, whether she was "royal" or not, and there was nothing else. We got the same people in every world including her family, we got Marguerite jumping worlds to find out about her fathers real killer, and we got no creativity anywhere. I can't really see why people enjoy this. There were also some typing errors or was that just the book <i>I read?</i> The rest of the book was really just about Marguerite falling for Paul Markov, but it wasn't <b>her Paul,</b> it was Paul from Russia, the caring oh-so handsome and nice Paul that would call Her Imperial Highness <i>My lady</i> and would speak to her in such a formal way even when they had kissed, had sex, and she had told him to call her by Marguerite. Maybe there's character development in the other book, and maybe Marguerite chooses her boyfriend, or did she already choose him in this one? The love triangle really didn't bother me, I kind of knew who she was gonna pick. With that being said, I'm surprised again that I finished this and didn't DNF it. Overall, I just don't think Claudia Gray's books are for me. Her <i>Evernight</i> series doesn't intrigue me and have my attention either. I'll probably read the other book, but not soon. I'll be skipping Gray's other books as well. Her writing isn't for me, her characters feel boring and underdeveloped to me, and the unneeded conversations feel awkward. <br /><br /><b>Sorry to the ones who enjoyed this, love it and find it brilliant and amazing and awesome, but it's another 1 star for me. I should've seen this coming.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11739042029479882303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1540942699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540942699" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540942699?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540942699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3154692131785508623">Edit: I read this again while on holiday and it's still fantastic. Has there ever been a fictional man more perfect than Paul? I don't think so. He is simply incomparable.<br/><br/>Not to be Unpopular Opinions Angela, but I'm going to have to swim against the tide with this one. I know that a lot of people think this book is shite, but I'm here, I'm queer, and I'm ready to stand up on my soapbox and yell at all of you through a crackly loudspeaker: I loved this book. <br/><br/>I loved my salty daughter Marguerite, </span>
  <span id="freeText3154692131785508623" style="display:none">Edit: I read this again while on holiday and it's still fantastic. Has there ever been a fictional man more perfect than Paul? I don't think so. He is simply incomparable.<br /><br />Not to be Unpopular Opinions Angela, but I'm going to have to swim against the tide with this one. I know that a lot of people think this book is shite, but I'm here, I'm queer, and I'm ready to stand up on my soapbox and yell at all of you through a crackly loudspeaker: I loved this book. <br /><br />I loved my salty daughter Marguerite, with her grand gestures and her dramatic inner monologue and her total disregard for the consequences of her foolish actions (insert: that Vine where the kid screams "when will you learn that your actions have <i>consequences?</i>" RIP Vine, you'll always be remembered with a fond little chuckle and a jaunty head tilt). <br /><br />I could have done without Theo, but he did add another dimension to this (ha ha ha) and, having read the rest of this series, his character is a lovely and complex shade of grey. In particular, his relationship with Paul was this edgy, dangerous thing, barbed at the edges. He belittles Paul fondly, as "brothers" do, but with that underlying slant of jealousy that invites unsavoury questions. I like that. <br /><br />Speaking of Paul: I mean, what can I say? Paul is my husband and we're happily married. Thank you. We registered for gifts at TK Maxx Home and the Bohemians (you'll have to travel for the latter, but I've got my eye on that big clay oil pot). I love everything about him and if you come to my house for a bevy I'll set up my projector and show you my Powerpoint that details the 96 reasons why. The abridged version is that Paul is perfection and I will defend him until my dying breath. <br /><br />This book was a blast, and so is the rest of the series. It's unique, it's flashy, it's paced so frenetically but with just the right balance of conversational prose. It does something interesting with its characters, too: nobody's the good guy, and nobody's evil. It's grey, it's complicated, and we've all got to live with the uneasy notion that, had the trajectory of our lives been angled slightly differently, we might not be who we are now. For me, that was a concept that blew this book out of the water. It makes this series compulsively readable, time and time again. <br /><br />Good job, Claudia Gray. And thanks for bringing Paul into my life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3154692131785508623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1257077892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257077892" />
    <a title="Anja H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h"><img alt="Anja H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559051853p2/6054186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257077892?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja H." href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h">Anja H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257077892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8365046332910145556"><b>*2 AVERAGE STARS*</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>"Every form of art is another way of seeing the world."</b>
</i><br/><br/>Let me just cut right to the chase: I didn't like this book. <br/>When I first read the plot and saw the <b>stunning</b> cover, I thought this was going to be awesome and badass but in the end this book left me really disappointed. The whole plot with the time travel and different dimensions could have been really interesting, but the author didn't use it to their full potential in my opinion. So much more could've happened but this</span>
  <span id="freeText8365046332910145556" style="display:none"><b>*2 AVERAGE STARS*</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Every form of art is another way of seeing the world."</b>
</i><br /><br />Let me just cut right to the chase: I didn't like this book. <br />When I first read the plot and saw the <b>stunning</b> cover, I thought this was going to be awesome and badass but in the end this book left me really disappointed. The whole plot with the time travel and different dimensions could have been really interesting, but the author didn't use it to their full potential in my opinion. So much more could've happened but this book only contained three dimensions, in which Marguerite started this weird love quadrangle involving Theo and two Pauls (yeah, you read that right), and it left me completely confused.<br /><br />I can't really put my finger on what exactly I didn't like about this. I mean, I definitely loved the whole idea of time travel, but not the way they went about it. The first 100 started off quite good, but it all went downhill from the moment Marguerite caught Paul. <i>Claudia Gray</i>'s writing style was good, but not great. Every time Marguerite changed dimensions, I felt like she was running away from the problems she caused in the previous one.<br />And even though all the characters in this book are older than some of the other young adult book characters out there, they somehow seemed really juvenile and <b>childish</b> to me, especially with all the dumb decisions they made.<br /><br />The one character I really liked is Russia's Lieutenant Paul Markov, I mean, he's just so sweet and not as distant as the original one, but oh man, I didn't like the insta-love-thing that happened between him and Marguerite. And then when she feels attracted to the Paul from her own dimension, which I don't get because he's an antisocial awkward turtle, she thinks that she's cheating on the Russian one.. I mean, <i>come on!</i> I do like Theo as a character but I don't really ship Marguerite with anyone, which is weird for me because I'm usually an avid shipper. I just didn't really connect with any of the characters.<br /><br />Honestly, I found the whole story to be quite <b>boring</b>. There was way too much focus on the weird romance and not enough action and suspense. This book ends with a happy ending, so I'm really unsure about what they'll do with the next two books, as it seems like this is going to be a trilogy. <br />Since I've decided that I'm only going to be reading books and series I really <b>want</b> to read from now on, I won't torture myself with trying to continue this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8365046332910145556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10502567-jiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802437462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7374117128847043977">Aaaaaand another review that's almost 2 weeks late. <br/><br/><b>Initial reaction to this book:</b> KFKSDH;KHDSA;KHDFKDHFKDJSHF DKHDSKNDNDAUIRHAIEONCDSNCKHF EUHFEHAFHJDHFKDSHFDHNC HEHFFDHSDAHSIAEAIDSJ ANFC KDSNVFAHFISAHF AIEIFJADFIEAFDSFHAE<br/><br/><b>Current reaction to this book:</b> KFKSDH;KHDSA;KHDFKDHFKDJSHF DKHDSKNDNDAUIRHAIEONCDSNCKHF EUHFEHAFHJDHFKDSHFDHNC HEHFFDHSDAHSIAEAIDSJ ANFC KDSNVFAHFISAHF AIEIFJADFIEAFDSFHAE<br/><br/>I've been wanting to read this book for so, so long! I admit I only originally added it because of the cov</span>
  <span id="freeText7374117128847043977" style="display:none">Aaaaaand another review that's almost 2 weeks late. <br /><br /><b>Initial reaction to this book:</b> KFKSDH;KHDSA;KHDFKDHFKDJSHF DKHDSKNDNDAUIRHAIEONCDSNCKHF EUHFEHAFHJDHFKDSHFDHNC HEHFFDHSDAHSIAEAIDSJ ANFC KDSNVFAHFISAHF AIEIFJADFIEAFDSFHAE<br /><br /><b>Current reaction to this book:</b> KFKSDH;KHDSA;KHDFKDHFKDJSHF DKHDSKNDNDAUIRHAIEONCDSNCKHF EUHFEHAFHJDHFKDSHFDHNC HEHFFDHSDAHSIAEAIDSJ ANFC KDSNVFAHFISAHF AIEIFJADFIEAFDSFHAE<br /><br />I've been wanting to read this book for so, so long! I admit I only originally added it because of the cover. Can we take a moment (or 10 moments) to appreciate the cover? It's hands-down one of the best covers I've seen!! I bought the first two books a while back and they've been sitting on my shelf since then. I finally decided to read book 1. And my friends, <b>I should've read it sooner.</b><br /><br />I love time travel. I haven't read many novels with that theme, but I love it. The world-building of this novel was spectacular. I love the many concepts Claudia Gray managed to include and how she gradually made them all clearer as the story progressed (there's so much Physics in them!). I loved the many verses this story had; my favorite most definitely being the Russiaverse. Oh my God. I smiled like an idiot, laughed, swooned, and cried reading that verse. It had it all! Such a perfect verse.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I would love you in any shape, in any world, with any past. Never doubt that.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Yes, this book has a love triangle. Is it annoying? For me, no. I've stated many times that love triangles don't bother me if they're done right. This is the case here. <br /><br /><b>Paul Markov. Theo Beck.</b> AAAAAAAAAAA THESE TWO! I love them both so much I want to protect them.<br /><br />And the big twist... oh damn that big twist! I was left so shook by it! I didn't expect it at all. The pacing was great, the plot was crazy and I just want more, more, more.<br /><br />Prepare to be amazed when you read this book! You'll smile, laugh, be shocked, and cry. It has it all. <br /><br />I rarely start sequels directly after. I usually like to take a small break between sequels. But here... I was so happy I already had book two and I quickly dove right into it!<br /><br /><b>Highly recommended.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7374117128847043977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1037270479?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="vicky." class="user" itemprop="url" name="vicky." href="/user/show/22094171-vicky">vicky.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13914414778225813657"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769099.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769100.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, I've read a couple of Claudia Gray's books and enjoyed them, but what the fuck is this? <br/> <br/>Marguerite's parents are geniuses who built a device called the Firebird, that allows people to travel to parallel universes. But then her father is murdered and their assistant Paul is the only suspect. But wait, he also stole the Firebirds! So Meg joins her BFF Theo (who also works with her parents, how convenient) in a quest for revenge.<br/> <br/>Don't get too excited though, it's less:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769101.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>or mayb</span>
  <span id="freeText13914414778225813657" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769099.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769100.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don't get me wrong, I've read a couple of Claudia Gray's books and enjoyed them, but what the fuck is this? <br> <br>Marguerite's parents are geniuses who built a device called the Firebird, that allows people to travel to parallel universes. But then her father is murdered and their assistant Paul is the only suspect. But wait, he also stole the Firebirds! So Meg joins her BFF Theo (who also works with her parents, how convenient) in a quest for revenge.<br> <br>Don't get too excited though, it's less:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769101.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>or maybe <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769102.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>actually there's a lot of:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411180225ra/11202216.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book had so much potential I AM ANGRY. The explanation for the parallel universes is that they are around us but just can't see them<br>...<br> <br>This is YA so of course there are two love interests. Theo who is hilarious, easy-going and super hot, and Paul who is shy, quiet and mysterious. <br>But at the beginning of the book she isn't in love with either of them, she just wants revenge! So she makes the first jump and ends up in a high-tech London, she manages to track Paul and when she confronts him, demanding to know why he killed her dad.. <br> <br> <blockquote>
  <i>“What?” His face pales so suddenly that I think for a moment he might pass out. “What—you said—Henry’s dead? He’s dead?”<br>The astonishment and pain I see are very real. Some people are good enough actors to feign shock, but shy, uncertain Paul Markov has never had that kind of game. There’s no way he could fake this kind of horror, or the tears I can see welling in his eyes.<br>It hits me then, a blow more stupefying than sharp: Paul didn’t kill my father.</i>
</blockquote><br> <br>She just simply believes he didn't do it BECAUSE HIS EYES GOT SAD :(<br>So Paul escapes (yeah again) and Meg follows him. They end up in Russia, or a version of it, where Meg is a tsarevna, a princess.<br>Long story short, she falls in love with the Paul of that universe (let's call him R!Paul). No, not in love, she truly loves him even though they met each other for two weeks. But maybe R!Meg loves him too so is okay! <br> <br>But the thing that annoyed the fuck out of me is that in every single chapter Meg remembers Paul, the way he used to be around her, how he looked; and with every motherfucker chapter she slowly falls in love.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769103.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nevermind that he killed her father (but he didn't do it remember? he got sad eyes :( ) or that she left her grieving mother and sister just to find him and get justice. No, perhaps she was in love all this time, she just realized now... Awful timing, this girl.<br> <br><blockquote>
  <i>I fell in love with one Paul. I fell in love with his unchanging soul. Does that mean I fell in love with every Paul, everywhere?</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418393731ra/12769104.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1777828534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777828534" />
    <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren"><img alt="Wren (fablesandwren)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596719528p2/42780417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777828534?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=03-stars">03-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=physical-shelf">physical-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=want-to-reread">want-to-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777828534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12153494942189020823">Okay, okay. Am I the only one who gets <b>really freaked out</b> when books <u>DON’T</u> end in a cliff hanger? Like I know there are other books after this series but this book ended on a more than mildly happy note. So I feel like… super calm and just want to know what is going to electrocute me / drown me / tear me apart in the books to come. <br/><br/>That’s probably just my anxiety talking.<br/><br/>So this very artsy girl (Marguerite) has two super brainiac parents who invent this gadget that can take you to different-yet-</span>
  <span id="freeText12153494942189020823" style="display:none">Okay, okay. Am I the only one who gets <b>really freaked out</b> when books <u>DON’T</u> end in a cliff hanger? Like I know there are other books after this series but this book ended on a more than mildly happy note. So I feel like… super calm and just want to know what is going to electrocute me / drown me / tear me apart in the books to come. <br><br>That’s probably just my anxiety talking.<br><br>So this very artsy girl (Marguerite) has two super brainiac parents who invent this gadget that can take you to different-yet-parallel universe. There are zillions. What I gathered is that every time there is a decision and you make one, another universe is made with you making the other decision which could spiral into a completely different world with different progresses in technology.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512868133ra/24640010.gif" alt="" width="350" height="196" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know, now you are thinking “so when I decided to brush my teeth this morning, there was all of a sudden another universe where I didn’t?” Okay, I don’t think those particular one’s count per-say BUT hey, what do I know? I’m not <a>Claudia Gray</a>, aka the woman I believe is going to ruin me.<br><br>So anyway, Marguerite and her sister basically have adoptive siblings. Wait no, we can’t say that because LOW AND BEHOLD THERE IS A LOVE TRIANGLE. How about Marguerite’s parents adopt Theo and Paul and they are nothing like siblings to Marguerite at all? Yah… yah, let’s go with that. <br><br>So someone killed Marguerite’s father. And that someone seems to be Paul. The kicker is that Paul took a firebird (that thing that allows them to jump dimensions and into ‘themselves’ in that dimension) and escaped before he could be caught.<br><br>Marguerite is absolutely crushed (duh, it was her dad) and convinces Theo to let her go along with him to go and find Paul, bring him back, and actually probably maybe kill him because she is so <b>infuriated</b>.<br><br>So then there is a twist, then there is a twist in the twist, then there is a twist within the twist that twisted before and then when you look really REALLY closely, you can see that there is an explosion of twist right there in the center of it all.<br><br>Bringing it back.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512868133ra/24640012.gif" alt="" width="350" height="197" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Things I absolutely loved:<br>1.	We visit so many awesome places. Like futuristic London, Medieval Russia to air-bowl-in-the-ocean-progressed-science land. <br>2.	You actually get to see the pain of losing a parent with Marguerite. Now, I myself have not lost a parent thankfully, but I believe it isn’t something that you can just forget. Especially when your parallel-self has that parent still. <br>3.	Some of the twist I saw coming <b>AND SOME I ABSOLUTELY DIDN’T</b>.<br><br>Things I could have done without:<br>1.	The ever-fan-favorite love triangle.<br>Now two things on this. One, if you are anything like me, you don’t really see one as the obvious choice. I mean, Marguerite ends up with who she saw as the obvious choice, but I, for some reason, don’t see that choice sticking very well. I am not sure why and I could be completely off track. That is something I do like about it though, that it isn’t a Edward/Jacob thing where you know she is going to end up with ****.<br>Two, I know we are all tired of love triangles, but that does make things interesting for books so I see why they do it.<br>2.	I wish the romance was less of the focus for this book. Romance isn’t a particular genre that I feel pulled to, even though I have read a lot of romance and fallen in love with certain books. I like the down in the dirt and gravel type of books where the action stays tall and the story gets bigger and bigger. This story is probably going to blow up in my face here soon, but the action was lacking for my taste.<br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed getting into this book and I am itching to get my hands on the next one to figure out which way my heart is going to break and my brain is going to explode. If I was a betting girl, I would say that the action picks up. The book was leaning that way. But then again, it ended really happy. <br><br>It’s going to get bad. <br><br>I’m so ready.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512868133ra/24640009.gif" alt="" width="350" height="196" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12153494942189020823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_939624031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939624031" />
    <a title="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit"><img alt="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448295560p2/4163146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939624031?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" href="/user/show/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit">Tiff at Mostly YA Lit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939624031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13852969694071078954">Holy cow, <b>A Thousand Pieces of You was a serious ride</b>.<br/><br/>What works so well in this book is that author Claudia Gray s<b>ets up the very complex world building, then spins philosophy, art, mystery and romance around it</b>. There are so many threads here to think about, and the story deftly switches between them. Except for a bit of confusion and clunkiness I felt at the beginning with all the exposition (this book really does start in media res), the story flowed smoothly, with a ton of twists and turns.</span>
  <span id="freeText13852969694071078954" style="display:none">Holy cow, <b>A Thousand Pieces of You was a serious ride</b>.<br><br>What works so well in this book is that author Claudia Gray s<b>ets up the very complex world building, then spins philosophy, art, mystery and romance around it</b>. There are so many threads here to think about, and the story deftly switches between them. Except for a bit of confusion and clunkiness I felt at the beginning with all the exposition (this book really does start in media res), the story flowed smoothly, with a ton of twists and turns. <b>Every time I thought I knew what was happening, it turned out that Gray was already two steps ahead of me. </b><br><br>I also loved how much time we got to spend figuring out the different universes, how they were different and how they were similar to Marguerite's own world. For instance, in one universe, John Lennon and Paul McCartney never met, so the Beatles didn't exist; instead, Paul and George Harrison form a band called The Gears. <b>Little details really made the different worlds believable. </b><br><br>If I had to nitpick a little, I would probably say that the<b> character work could have been more developed</b> in this book - the characters definitely suffered a bit in service to plot, theme, and world-building. I felt like I was told how amazing Marguerite was, but I didn't really see it as much as I should have - I knew she was an artist, but it was hard for me to tell if she was funny or silly or serious. I also felt like the guys were archetypes: Paul was the silent, mysterious boy, while Theo was the bad boy with the good heart. I wish I'd known more about them than just that. I'm looking forward to finding out more in book 2, though, and honestly, this is one of those books where the plot necessarily carries you forward.<br>Here's the thing: I fully admit that I did not expect this book to live up to its epically fantastic cover. I mean, look at that gorgeousness! But guys, let me tell you: it does. <b>This book slayed me in twenty different ways, and I can't wait to get my hands on book 2. </b><br> <br>Bonuses: <br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://api.ning.com/files/uY3PJt2fxPzbEvQAMTazPPf2X8t97WXMqnf0IuZy-nRLZRYag-5r4KhhMCW*UaMdpZARVUYP45ZaFM*2KYmIUh1LLtJYresC/animation.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415112955ra/11727002.gif" height="200" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><b>Addictive Writing:</b> Writing-wise, I was really impressed by Gray's vivid descriptions, and the way she could turn those at a moment's notice into heart-pounding action. There was a great balance of beautiful writing and writing that kept me on the edge of my seat. The action scenes reminded me of how I felt when I read Divergent the first time - I was totally hooked.<br><div>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-UbjDt_-3tj4/VFhwRekOzzI/AAAAAAAACfU/1SXmbn_Lx1E/s1600/sexytimes.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415112955i/11727003.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><b>Sexy Times:</b> I can't talk about this book without talking about the steamy romance going on. There are some seriously sexy times here - for younger readers and parents, just know that there are a few moments of R-rated-ness. Those moments are lush and added a lot to my emotional investment in the story.<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-syDTQL_QG3c/UtK3BOU4yeI/AAAAAAAAB34/rbScdIBMSLc/s1600/I_heart_question_mark_by_JONASADDICT2.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415112955i/11727004.jpg" height="200" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><b>Love Triangle That Works:</b> The love interests in this book really worked for me - in part because they are so different, but equally good choices. This isn't a case where you're going to be Team Paul or Team Theo immediately (and heck, the triangle gets even more complicated because of the different versions of characters that are jumping into each others' bodies). This genuinely feels like two guys who really like this girl and it really is her choice.<br><br> 
  <b><br>The Final Word: </b>
 <br>A Thousand Pieces of You is so many kinds of awesome. <b>There's a bit of everything in this book: romance, adventure, suspense, mystery, time travel, historical, sci-fi</b>...trust me when I say that you need this one on your TBR immediately. It's definitely one of the most fun and addictive reads I've had in awhile, and I will definitely be re-reading certain bits over and over again.<br><br><b>Recommended for:</b> fans of Every Day or Cloud Atlas (both very apt comparisons), people who like time travel or sci-fi reads, people who like genre-benders<br><br>Review originally posted at <a href="http://mostlyyalit.blogspot.ca/2014/11/a-thousand-pieces-of-you-claudia-gray.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mostly YA Lit</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13852969694071078954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1591332124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1591332124" />
    <a title="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books"><img alt="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527965221p2/19967008.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" href="/user/show/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books">Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books?shelf=btb-challenge-2017">btb-challenge-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books?shelf=favorite-covers">favorite-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1591332124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7045143392914601312">Not gonna lie, A Thousand Pieces of You was a book I added to my TBR list solely for it’s cover. I didn’t even read the description of the book before I added it because the cover it so gorgeous! I mean really, just look at it! It might be one of my favorite covers ever – I’m kind of obsessed with it. That said, I’m SO glad I decided to read it because I looooved the book!<br/><br/>Marguerite grew up with physicists for parents, so she’s no stranger to experiments and gadgets strewn about her house. Her p</span>
  <span id="freeText7045143392914601312" style="display:none">Not gonna lie, A Thousand Pieces of You was a book I added to my TBR list solely for it’s cover. I didn’t even read the description of the book before I added it because the cover it so gorgeous! I mean really, just look at it! It might be one of my favorite covers ever – I’m kind of obsessed with it. That said, I’m SO glad I decided to read it because I looooved the book!<br /><br />Marguerite grew up with physicists for parents, so she’s no stranger to experiments and gadgets strewn about her house. Her parents and their research assistants Paul and Theo develop a device that they call the Firebird that allows people to jump through different dimensions. This invention is set to change science forever…until her dad is killed and Paul appears to be the killer. Paul takes off to another dimension, and Marguerite and Paul quickly follow, hoping to get justice for her father. Before long, Marguerite starts doubting Paul’s guilt, and begins to realize her feelings for him. As she jumps through dimensions, she begins to learn there was far more to her father’s death than she ever could have imagined…<br /><br />Let me just say again, I loved this book! I’ve never read a book with the same concept, so that made it unique for me. I really enjoyed that the book was told with a scientific mindset, similar to Dark Matter. There was a lot of talk about the science and physics that allowed Marguerite to jump between dimensions but it was never overwhelming to the point where I was confused. I also likes that there were rules put in place, such as not being able to jump backward or forward in time, or to dimensions where Marguerite hadn’t been born.<br /><br />There was a brief time where I thought we were going to end up with a love triangle, and I got slightly annoyed for a few minutes, worrying that we had another young woman who fell in love with any man who showed her attention, HOWEVER, the author did a great job at making Marguerite quickly learn who she actually had feelings for without dragging that decision out. I appreciated that.<br /><br />I found myself really engaged in the story and I was dying to find out where the story would go and whether or not Marguerite would make it home safely. All of my questions were answered and the resolution of this book set the second book up perfectly, without leaving us with a huge cliffhanger. I cannot wait to read book two – I’m planning to start it tonight so I can find out what happens next! I definitely recommend this one to fans of YA sci-fi who are looking for an adventurous story!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7045143392914601312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2727073601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2727073601" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2727073601?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">actual teen readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=romancelandia">romancelandia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2727073601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9040637677043332103">Although I wouldn't have read or finished this book if it weren't my book club's pick, I didn't hate <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17234658.A_Thousand_Pieces_of_You__Firebird___1_' title='A Thousand Pieces of You (Firebird, #1) by Claudia Gray' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Thousand Pieces of You</a>.<br/><br/>I sometimes forget that YA novels are actually written for TEENS, not middle-aged women like me. I don't know why other adults read YA, but I read teen books mostly because some of them are outstanding works of art.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17234658.A_Thousand_Pieces_of_You__Firebird___1_' title='A Thousand Pieces of You (Firebird, #1) by Claudia Gray' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Thousand Pieces of You</a> however is not a work of art, it has no adult cross-over appeal, it's not intellectually or morally challenging, and it doesn't try to</span>
  <span id="freeText9040637677043332103" style="display:none">Although I wouldn't have read or finished this book if it weren't my book club's pick, I didn't hate <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17234658.A_Thousand_Pieces_of_You__Firebird___1_" title="A Thousand Pieces of You (Firebird, #1) by Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Pieces of You</a>.<br><br>I sometimes forget that YA novels are actually written for TEENS, not middle-aged women like me. I don't know why other adults read YA, but I read teen books mostly because some of them are outstanding works of art.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17234658.A_Thousand_Pieces_of_You__Firebird___1_" title="A Thousand Pieces of You (Firebird, #1) by Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Pieces of You</a> however is not a work of art, it has no adult cross-over appeal, it's not intellectually or morally challenging, and it doesn't try to be. It's a story aimed at teens, and if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1192311.Claudia_Gray" title="Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">Claudia Gray</a> knows anything, it is how to write for her audience. The final product is an adventure story with the most popular type of a teen protagonist ever - a bland, but super speshul girl who is hunted by moustache-twirling villains and loved by not just two hot guys, but also EVERY VERSION OF THESE TWO GUYS IN EVERY PARALLEL WORLD she ever visits in this multiverse fantasy. I see why this scenario works for the readers, I really do.<br><br>And speaking of multiverse? Who doesn't like a multiverse scenario? From Sliders to Fringe, to Sliding Doors and Run Lola Run and Edge of Tomorrow. His Dark Materials and Life After Life... There is so much of this trope to love, in so many iterations.<br><br>Does <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17234658.A_Thousand_Pieces_of_You__Firebird___1_" title="A Thousand Pieces of You (Firebird, #1) by Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Pieces of You</a> have anything remarkable to offer? Eh, not to me. The world building is weak. There are parallel worlds where nothing seems to be different from the real world, another appears to be different in only the existence of a tPhone instead of an iPhone. <br><br>The most developed (if you can call it that) is the world I was most interested in (for reason of liking to rant about depictions of Russia in American lit) is the Pre-Industrial Russia where Marguerite is a Grand Duchess. And here Claudia Gray did something truly brilliant, if you think the goal of world building is to make the least number of factual mistakes. She established this "Russian" world by using just a handful of Russia-adjacent words - snow, tsar, caviar, fur coat/hat, borscht, dacha, Faberge eggs. (No bears, no balalaikas? My, I am disappointed!) She gave her characters Russian names, and spelled and used them correctly! I am even willing to overlook the fact that all these characters are supposed to be addressed by their first+middle name (for example, Marguerite should have been called Margarita Alexandrovna). But I get it, this is WAY too hard. <br><br>The only real error I noticed is the use of the word "golubka" (Russian for "dove"). You see, Russian words have "genders" - there are feminine, masculine and neutral nouns. "Golubka" is a feminine noun. So you can use it to address Marguerite, but not Paul. Paul would be "golub.'"<br><br>But all these things would not interest the book's real target audience. Neither would the aspects of this novel deserving of the most exploration - the ethical consequences of possessing other people's bodies, or the hardships of being in the worlds with foreign languages spoken or serving in absolutely unknown professions. The ease with witch Gray resolves these difficulties is quite remarkable. You end up in a body of a British person, oh, no worries, your body miraculously remembers to speak with a British accent. You are in a body of a Russian princess - yeah, your body knows and understands Russian for you. You are supposed to ride a submarine - can you believe it, one of your boyfriends has JUST taken a submarine simulation course! Ugh. <br><br>Instead readers get a competently crafted story that moves along quickly and provides a multitude of opportunities for Marguerite to touch and swoon over and fall into beds with her 2 (3,4,5? I am honestly not sure at this point) love interests, consequences to the bodies they "wear" be damned. <br><br>Not for me.<br><br>May I suggest this Netflix's recent multiverse-like experience to those who, like me, want something fresher and richer and juicier to sink teeth into? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551281956i/27125889._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9040637677043332103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2453355854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2453355854" />
    <a title="Lo O&#39;Neill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61150031-lo-o-neill"><img alt="Lo O&#39;Neill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522751586p2/61150031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2453355854?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lo O&#39;Neill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lo O&#39;Neill" href="/user/show/61150031-lo-o-neill">Lo O&#39;Neill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61150031-lo-o-neill?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61150031-lo-o-neill?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61150031-lo-o-neill?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2453355854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12939879569949057684">I would be lying if I said that the cover of this book was 80% of the reason that I picked it up. Like come on look at it! It is beautiful! Thankfully, when I started reading the book I was as enraptured by story as much as I was with the cover.<br/><br/><i>A Thousand Pieces of You</i> comes off the starting blocks with a speed that I did not expect. Gray doesn’t spend the first few chapters building the world and introducing the characters instead the reader is thrust into this world where inter-dimensional tra</span>
  <span id="freeText12939879569949057684" style="display:none">I would be lying if I said that the cover of this book was 80% of the reason that I picked it up. Like come on look at it! It is beautiful! Thankfully, when I started reading the book I was as enraptured by story as much as I was with the cover.<br /><br /><i>A Thousand Pieces of You</i> comes off the starting blocks with a speed that I did not expect. Gray doesn’t spend the first few chapters building the world and introducing the characters instead the reader is thrust into this world where inter-dimensional travel is possible and Grey catches us up with everything else along the ride. The pace works perfectly for the book as it fits with the flow the story, at times where she wants us to take a breather and get the know the characters she slows down the speed and at others we feel like we are on this wild ride together. <br /><br />The main focus of the story is inter-dimension travel and the possibilities with that and the author builds this possibility beautifully and intricately. It is so smartly delivered that I was left feeling like I didn’t have to suspend my disbelief for too long in order to get lost in the worlds created. Each world also felt complete and I got an entirely different feeling from each one, although I do have to say that I think the dimension where they are in Russia is my favourite one. This is my first foray into a story based on the muti-verse theory and I think this was a wonderful one to start with.<br /><br />I know that a lot of people hate on the love triangle trope that is in a lot of YA novels but I can admit that I am a sucker for them (unfortunately, I always seem to prefer the person that they don’t end up with - the only exception to that one is the Hunger Games!) so I can’t pretend that I didn’t enjoy the dynamics created in this love triangle, made all the more interesting with the different presentations of the characters in the different dimensions. One of the reason that I think that love triangles are so hated on is because they tend to get dragged out for a little too long, especially when a book is part of a series. Thankfully, <i>A Thousand Pieces of You</i> does not fall into this trap and the whole book is not consumed with the love triangle. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ My heart did break when Russian Paul died, I just was not expecting that and was not prepared to deal with the emotions! I really need to learn to stop reading books in the canteen on my lunch breaks, I should know that if the story is good I will get too caught up in it!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b> 5 Stars</b> for <i>A Thousand Pieces of You</i> and I can’t wait to read the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12939879569949057684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2070287497?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen">Maureen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2070287497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16887764797266920309">5th for Booktubeathon 2017 DOWN!<br/><br/>Some 3 books are just meh I didn't like it, but this is one where there are things I intensely liked and things that I just as intensely disliked. <br/>The whole concept of this book was fascinating but when we finally started getting into the plot? Was so boring. Nothing was moving or happening and it felt like it just switched to a historical fiction book instead of a sci-fi. There were also lots of tropes including one of my least favorite ones, and it was VERY pred</span>
  <span id="freeText16887764797266920309" style="display:none">5th for Booktubeathon 2017 DOWN!<br /><br />Some 3 books are just meh I didn't like it, but this is one where there are things I intensely liked and things that I just as intensely disliked. <br />The whole concept of this book was fascinating but when we finally started getting into the plot? Was so boring. Nothing was moving or happening and it felt like it just switched to a historical fiction book instead of a sci-fi. There were also lots of tropes including one of my least favorite ones, and it was VERY predictable, but I still ended up liking this book?<br />Even though the plot was not all there at first it really really came together in the end. I also liked how one trope I'm tired of seeing was really turned on it's head and made into something different. The characters and the concept of fate that was explored in this book were both so great. Even if the romance HEAVILY overshadowed the plot so so so many times. And even though I was annoyed at the once section that felt heavily like historical fiction, I still loved that world. <br />All in all, a really interesting book that has convinced me to at least carry on with the series.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hrJLTHRgmufetxff6IinkWrXgnxK0Q8ypb3qvYk+cK2EjhenVuVamJ9hfYoNKf8x1ZYX9sV47ae4ZGckJzOFLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NIJZ/J//uksgQwP9UWek3hbjBbS/FXsVw0XgGRq0Sac2vgUXvXp6NGGVaai0xvx+qaKQPjC8mYDenG2AtLm8Jw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText17257390765300580915" style="display:none">Claudia Gray is not my real name. I didn't choose a pseudonym because my real name is unpleasant (it isn't), because I'd always dreamed of calling myself this (I haven't) or even because I'm hiding from the remnants of that international diamond-smuggling cartel I smashed in 2003 (Interpol has taken care of them). In short, I took a pseudonym for no real reason whatsoever. Sometimes this is actually the best reason to do things.<br /><br />I live in New Orleans. So far, in life, I've been a disc jockey, a lawyer, a journalist and an extremely bad waitress, just to name a few. I especially like to spend time traveling, hiking, reading and listening to music. More than anything else, I enjoy writing. <br /></span>
